## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics & constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in thermo-mechanics (elasticity, plasticity, viscoelasticity) where stiffness, yield stress, and hardening/softening depend on T and deformation level.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke with T-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elasticity with stiffness changing with temperature)
- Polynomial elastic law (nonlinear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (hyperelastic/anharmonic elastic response at larger strains)
- Thermal-stress offset (thermal strain folded into intercept): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T) (effective stress shifting with temperature-induced strain/misfit)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally activated reduction/increase of stiffness; sign of c1 sets softening/hardening)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic (idealized yield with hardening): sigma = Min(c0 * epsilon, c1 + c2 * (epsilon - c3)) (elastic regime then plastic flow/hardening; symbolic form often approximated smoothly)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (plastic strain hardening; c1 can represent strain offset)
- Ludwik-type hardening with yield offset: sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield stress plus strain hardening)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit, often rearranged/approximated): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition; can be inverted approximately to sigma(epsilon))
- Saturating hardening (Voce-type in strain): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that approaches a saturation stress)
- T-dependent yield stress with hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * (epsilon + c3)**c4 (temperature-dependent yield plus strain hardening)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable form (common in metals): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3) * (c4 + c5 * T) (strain hardening multiplied by thermal softening/hardening factor)
- Arrhenius-like thermal activation expressed as exp in T (without 1/T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3) * exp(c4 * T) (empirical/limited-range thermally activated flow stress approximation)
- Rational saturation in strain with thermal scaling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (epsilon + c2) (initially linear, then saturating stress with temperature-dependent scale)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → use a separable product: sigma = E(T) * epsilon with E(T) as (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) or exp(c * T).
- Thermal softening of flow stress → multiplicative temperature factor on a hardening term, e.g., sigma = H(epsilon) * exp(c * T) with c < 0.
- Yield-like behavior in sigma(epsilon) → structures with an intercept plus nonlinear growth, e.g., sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3, indicating a nonzero stress at near-zero strain (offset/yield).
- Finite hardening capacity (saturation) → use sigma approaching an asymptote via (1 - exp(c * epsilon)) or rational forms epsilon/(epsilon + c).
- Elastic–plastic transition region → combine an approximately linear term with a higher-order/power term (additive) to capture curvature between regimes.
- Thermal strain/misfit effects folded into strain → use shifted strain (epsilon + c * T) inside the constitutive nonlinearity.
- Strain-rate-independent plasticity surrogates → prefer monotone convex hardening forms (power laws) over oscillatory functions; enforce sigma increasing with epsilon for stable hardening.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity → allow cross terms like (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 to capture temperature-dependent strain sensitivity.

The fitted c0≈-427.7 and c4≈-273.0 are extremely large in magnitude, so ε^2 and ε terms dominate and can overwhelm the nominal T*ε term unless ε is tiny; this suggests the polynomial part is doing most of the fitting. Approximate simplification: ε*(T - 273.0 + 7.75*sin(T+1.25)) - 427.7*ε^2.

### 3. `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon*sin(T*c3 + c4) + c5*epsilon`
